  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_12ece186-e5ab-4618-b204-d57788f0f10c'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText16625916159009407994" style="display:none"><i>"Magnus Chase, you nearly started Ragnarok. What are you going to do next?"</i><br /><br />It's been six weeks since Magnus and his friends returned from defeating Fenris Wolf and the fire giants. Magnus has adjusted to life at the Hotel Valhalla—as much as a once-homeless and previously alive kid can. As a son of Frey, the god of summer, fertility, and health, Magnus doesn't exactly fit in with the rest of Odin's chosen warriors, but he has a few good peeps among his hallmates on floor nineteen, and he's been dutifully training for Ragnarok along with everyone else. His days have settled into a new kind of normal.<br /><br />But Magnus should have known there's no such thing as normal in the Nine Worlds. His friends Hearthstone and Blitzen have disappeared. A new hallmate is creating chaos. According to a very nervous goat, a <i>certain object</i> belonging to Thor is still missing, and the thunder god's enemies will stop at nothing to gain control of it.<br /><br />Time to summon Jack, the Sword of Summer, and take action. Too bad the only action Jack seems to be interested in is dates with other magical weapons. . . .</span>

<span class='communityAnswererName'>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I love it. In my opinion, it's on an equal level with the others, though in a slightly different way which may be why it's not as popular. However, Sa<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I love it. In my opinion, it's on an equal level with the others, though in a slightly different way which may be why it's not as popular. However, Sadie has all the sass of Magnus and Percy, and Carter is a great character that takes after Annabeth's style of knowledge being power. They also have the same great chapter titles as PJO and Magnus Chase. Definitely recommend. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_2494576618" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2494576618" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2494576618?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141342566" href="/book/show/34879217-magnus-chase-and-the-hammer-of-thor">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2494576618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8928984540385176759"><i>”Just my luck, Grimwolf was happy to turn his attention to me. When it comes to drawing aggro from ancient monsters, I’ve got the golden touch.”</i><br/><br/>No kidding!!! Haha! I won’t even bother to try to make a list of the many ancient monsters Magnus pissed off in this book. Suffice it to say it were many. *lol* For some reason the gods seem to like him though so this is actually kind of funny and weird at the same time. XD<br/><br/>Well anyway, let’s talk about the book! This was such a typical Uncle Rick story a</span>
  <span id="freeText8928984540385176759" style="display:none"><i>”Just my luck, Grimwolf was happy to turn his attention to me. When it comes to drawing aggro from ancient monsters, I’ve got the golden touch.”</i><br /><br />No kidding!!! Haha! I won’t even bother to try to make a list of the many ancient monsters Magnus pissed off in this book. Suffice it to say it were many. *lol* For some reason the gods seem to like him though so this is actually kind of funny and weird at the same time. XD<br /><br />Well anyway, let’s talk about the book! This was such a typical Uncle Rick story and of course that immediately caused me to love every second of it. I don’t know how Uncle Rick does it but he has such an amazing imagination that everything seems to make sense even though it doesn’t. *lol* But then again I suppose that mythology is one of those things that rarely makes any sense and just the idea to use it as a basis for amazing fantasy books is actually more than just brilliant. ;-) <br /><br /><i>Heimdall laughed. “You have no idea. Once, I butt-dialled the apocalypse. So embarrassing. I had to text everybody on my contact list, like, False alarm! A lot of gods came running anyway. I made this GIF of them charging up the Bifrost and then realizing there was no battle. Priceless.”</i><br /><br />There, I said it. Uncle Rick you’re brilliant! XD You’re allowed to blush now, if that’s your kind of thing. ;-P<br /><br />And speaking of things: Another “thing” that’s always nice about Riordan’s books is that they are not only fast paced but have an amazing cast of diverse and multi-layered characters. They are certainly not your typical dwarf or elf and they all have very interesting and difficult background stories. This time around we found out more about Hearth’s past and Sam’s life and to say those two sub-plots were instructive would be more than just an understatement. <br /><br />Poor Sam had to go through a lot in this book and even though it must have been tough she still managed to deal with it somehow. Still, if she doesn’t start to rebel against her father soon all her awesome and faithful friends won’t be able to save her. She has to want this change otherwise it won’t work, so I really hope that she’ll take heart and decide to get help from Alex. =)<br /><br /><i>”She was betrothed to Amir. She loved the guy. I would raise an army of einherjar, magic elves and well-dressed dwarves and burn down Jotunheim before I let them coerce my friend.”</i><br /><br />And after mentioning Alex for the first time I can finally go into gushing mode!!!<br /><br /><b>
  <u>I LOVE ALEX FIERRO!!! &lt;333 </u>
</b><br /><br /><i>”What did you mean earlier?” I asked. “When you said –“<br />“Call me she? I’m gender fluid and transgender, idiot. Look it up if you need to, but it’s not my job to educate –“</i><br /><br />Thank you Uncle Rick!!! Thank you for introducing us to a gender fluid character!!! Alex is soo damn awesome I can’t even! I love her/his character and I’ll defend her/him with my life if necessary! She/he is precious and must be protected at all costs!!<br />Gosh, Uncle Rick I could kiss you for inventing Alex! If you want to collect that kiss you’ll have to come to Austria though. *lol* Well, and if you’re already at it, it wouldn’t hurt if you’d bring a signed copy of your book as well. Just saying. ;-P<br /><br /><i>”My pronouns are he and him,” Alex confirmed. “And you can stop staring.”<br />“I wasn’t …” I caught myself. Arguing would’ve been pointless.</i><br /><br />Also I love the idea that Alex might end up being Magnus love interest!!! I mean it’s pretty obvious that he likes her/him. All that blushing and feeling warm and fuzzy whenever she/he is around is enough reason to expect a ship to sail. And no, I’m not talking about <b>“The Ship of the Dead”</b> even though I’m pretty certain that we can expect <b>
  <u>THAT</u>
</b> ship to sail as well. *lol* Better don’t think about it. Dead peoples nails… Ewww!!! *shudders*<br /><br />Nope, I’d rather like Alex’s and Magnus’ ship to sail! Thank you very much! XD<br /><br />All told <b>“The Hammer of Thor”</b> was another amazing adventure and I can’t wait to read the final book of this trilogy! Give me all those intriguing background stories, suspenseful fights, weird and awkward moments and an adorable ship to sail! &lt;3<br />I want it all! ;-)</span>
  <a data-text-id="8928984540385176759" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1410820777?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="P " class="user" itemprop="url" name="P " href="/user/show/25327841-p">P </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1410820777" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15509725802390665619"><b>
  <blockquote>“Otis," I said.<br/>"Shhh," he said. "I'm incognito. Call me...Otis."<br/>"I'm not sure that's how incognito works, but okay."</blockquote>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1476286161i/20823236.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The Hammer of Thor is the second book of the series. The book starts off with the quest which is about Magnus finding Thor's hammer. He has to fight against the giants, his uncle and LOKI. BIG BAD LOKI. <i>AWWWW !</i> It looks promising, right ? And Alex is kinda kickass in this book. I liked her character, but not that much. Heart and Blitz are also my favorite characters, too. I hav</span>
  <span id="freeText15509725802390665619" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>“Otis," I said.<br>"Shhh," he said. "I'm incognito. Call me...Otis."<br>"I'm not sure that's how incognito works, but okay."</blockquote>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1476286161i/20823236.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The Hammer of Thor is the second book of the series. The book starts off with the quest which is about Magnus finding Thor's hammer. He has to fight against the giants, his uncle and LOKI. BIG BAD LOKI. <i>AWWWW !</i> It looks promising, right ? And Alex is kinda kickass in this book. I liked her character, but not that much. Heart and Blitz are also my favorite characters, too. I have lost count of the moments when I laughed and cried over them.<br><br>So why didn't I give this book five stars ?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1476286161ra/20823237.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Rick Riordan has done many things in these last ten years or so. The things that made me a fan of him was his humor and wonderful idea. The concept of Percy Jackson was new, fresh and vivid - it was easy to love that series. Then comes Carter and Percy Jackson season two. Honestly, because I grow up or other reasons, I didn't enjoy them as fully as possible. However, last year I gave the Magnus series a try and liked it a lot after that. I had had high expectations for this second book, I read it with twinkling stars in my heart. And then, nothing. I felt nothing after I finished this book. Although The Sword of Summer fired me up with its spectacular ending, The Hammer of Thor was another predicament.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“Mjolnir is always getting misplaced. I swear, Thor needs to have that hammer duct-taped to his face.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Rick recycled his plot. He polished the materials of his previous Percy books and mixed them up to be the new book showing before your eyes right now. The whole story was predictable. I'd known since the begining that<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Loki is to be released from his confinement. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> As why I was not excited and so lazy to finish. If I didn't get a lot of work to be done this weekend, I would put this book on hold until next month.<br><br>However, I still liked this. I want to know more about Magnus and his friends chasing after Loki and stopping Ragnarok. The next installment is going be mind-blowing ! I know it.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1476286343i/20823243.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Anyway, I was so curious why Thor didn't beckon to his hammer as in the movie...and it would come to his hand like this....<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444238444ra/16473291.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://goo.gl/6ZnIQI">https://goo.gl/6ZnIQI</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1623954676" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1623954676" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1623954676?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/29910798-magnus-chase-and-the-hammer-of-thor">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=ya-male-narrators">ya-male-narrators</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=magical-fantasy">magical-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=ya-without-romance">ya-without-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1623954676" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8943755129597232935">I mean <b>OBVIOUSLY I LOVED IT.</b> It's a Riordan book! What other emotions is a reader to have except: 40% laughing, 40% fangirling, and 20% thinking about falafel??? (There is <i>so</i> much falafel appreciation here, by the way. It's truly inspirational.) ANYWAY. I definitely thought this was another exciting and captivating instalment (although, still, like the first book...I think it got a bit rambly) and I loved the newly introduced characters and I <i>loved</i> how whacky all the gods were. And can we take a</span>
  <span id="freeText8943755129597232935" style="display:none">I mean <b>OBVIOUSLY I LOVED IT.</b> It's a Riordan book! What other emotions is a reader to have except: 40% laughing, 40% fangirling, and 20% thinking about falafel??? (There is <i>so</i> much falafel appreciation here, by the way. It's truly inspirational.) ANYWAY. I definitely thought this was another exciting and captivating instalment (although, still, like the first book...I think it got a bit rambly) and I loved the newly introduced characters and I <i>loved</i> how whacky all the gods were. And can we take a moment to just appreciate HOW HILARIOUS THESE BOOKS ARE??!? I LAUGH. I LAUGH AND LAUGH.<br /><br />Ahem.<br /><br /><b>So firstly, I have to yell about the characters.</b> There's just so much diversity here, that it's glorious. Plus all the secondary characters are enormously interesting and complex with a good dollop of TRAGIC. 3 <br /><br /><b>Magnus</b> of course remains a top-favourite...although at times (this might seem weird to say...) he nearly felt like a secondary character in this story?! It was honestly more about Loki's children and Magnus is child of Frey so...YEAH. But he has tons of sassy quips, he's such a sarcastic dork, and he gets a terrible haircut. So lovely. <br /><b>Sam</b> is still AWESOME although totally stubborn which gets them into a bit of puddles. Also I think it's adorable how in love she is with her betrothed Muslim boy, Amir. (And I'm still so insanely impressed there's no romance between her and Magus. YAAAAS.)<br />I also loved the introduction of <b>Alex Fierro</b>...but I was worried for a bit! Alex comes in really rude and snipy and, gah, I was just worried? BUT THEN ALEX ENDS UP BEING COMPLETELY AWESOME AND I LOVE ALEX. Also Alex is gender-fluid, but goes by he/she pronouns depending on the day. And like, I hope this is okay to say, but I really appreciated the open and blunt discussions on gender-fluidity. I think that'd be really helpful for kids who have questions (or maybe are discovering things about their sexuality/identity themselves) to be able to just read how Alex experiences their gender-fluidity OUTRIGHT without people being angry all the time at discussing it. Also <b>Alex is a shape-shifting child of Loki</b> so, like awesome is just in the top percentiles here.<br /><br />(SORRY I HAVE A SLIGHT SOFT SPOT FOR LOKI EVEN THOUGH HE'S EVIL HERE BUT HE'S ALSO TOM HIDDLESTON SO YEAH.)<br /><br /><b>I love the Sam/Magnus/Alex trio!!</b> (And of course we won't forget Hearth and Blitz the trusty sidekicks!) The dynamics, banter, and adventures surrounding them were <i>awesome</i>.<br /><br /><b>Also no romance?! wOOO!!</b> I have a <i>feeling</i> it'll be Magnus/Alex eventually? Magnus has done a lot of staring and kind of dropped his brain when he saw Alex in a really nice dress. SO. I predict....but so far, I would still say "No romance" for this book.<br /><br /><b>And I appreciate all the pop-culture references too.</b> IT'S HILARIOUS. (Although the book will be seriously dated in 10 years, but whatever.) When gods are taking selfies and watching Netflix, I'm just going to be over here enjoying myself okay?!<br /><br /><b>As for the actual plot?</b> It was like 80% awesome and 20% <i>"this is kind of a needless side-tour and why are we doing this get to the point mate"</i>. #awkward The quests (in this case, to find Thor's hammer) are always rambly...but sometimes I just want to CUT TO THE CHASE (hahhahhahaa...<i>get it?</i>?! Magnus <i>Chase</i>?? HAHAH. Yeah I'll shut up) instead of having a bowling competition with some giants. What can I say. I'm impatient.<br /><br />But we still met more hilarious ludicrous gods. Including more about Thor who's addicted to Netflix, and the guy who guards the bridge (I'm sorry...Norse spelling = me dead) being super into selfies. OH and we get more of Hearth's backstory and it's super tragic. POOR ELF.<br /><br /><b>ALL IN ALL:</b> It was a fabulously awesome hilarious and engaging story! I kept getting interrupted every time I sat down to read and YEAH I'M GONNA START CHUCKING HAMMERS IN A SECOND TOO. I weep 2 tears for the rambly plot and shout 8 hurrahs for how much I snickered. And then I'll just go pet the cover because the font is slightly raised and shiny and I'm in love with it. Book dragon, yo.<br /><br />*** QUOTES ***<br /><br /><blockquote>"Where have you been the last month and a half?"<br />Her shoulders tightened. "My workload this semester has been killing me. I'm tutoring kids after school. Then, as you might remember, there's my part-time job reaping souls of the dead and running top-secret mission for Odin."<br />"You kids today and your busy schedules."</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"Why doesn't Thor go check this barrow himself?" I asked. "Wait...let me guess. He doesn't want to draw attention. Or he wants us to have a chance to be heroes. Or it's hard work and he has some shows to catch up on."<br />"To be fair," Otis said, "the new season of <i>Jessica Jones</i> did just start streaming."</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>I flung him overhead. Jack spiralled out of view, flying after the goat-killer while singing his own version of "Shake It Off". (I have never been able to convince him that the line isn't <i>cheese graters gonna grate, grate, grate, grate, grate.)</i></blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"Where's the gold?" I demanded. "Don't make me unleash my sword's playlist."</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>Etiquette tip: if you're looking for the right time to leave a party, when the host yells "No one leaves here alive," that's your cue.</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"Your horn is a phone?" Amir asked.<br />"I think technically it's a phablet," Heimdall said. "But, yes, this is Gjallar, the Horn and/or Phablet of Doomsday! I blow this baby once, the gods know there's trouble in Asgard and they come running. I blow it <i>twice</i>, then it's Ragnarok, baby!" He seemed delighted by the idea that he could signal the start of the final battle that destroyed the Nine Worlds. "Most of the time, I just use it for photos and texting and whatnot."<br />"That's not scary at all," Alex said.<br />Heimdall laughed. "You have no idea. Once, I butt-dialled the apocalypse. <i>So</i> embarrassing. I had to text everybody on my contact lists, like, <i>False alarm!</i> A lot of gods came running anyway. I made this GIF of them charging up the Bifrost and then realising there was no battle. Priceless."</blockquote><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8943755129597232935" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1511867833" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1511867833" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1511867833?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141342559" href="/book/show/32021586-magnus-chase-and-the-hammer-of-thor">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=fantastic-lit-and-co">fantastic-lit-and-co</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1511867833" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer660208524609029996"><b>"At this point, most people would have thrown themselves down on the ground and given up hope. And by most people, I mean me."</b><br/><br/>•I know that I have already raved plenty about how much I love this author and his characters, but <b>Magnus Chase</b> defies all standards of cutie-pie-ness and adorable-ness and funny-ness and whatnot. You just cannot <i>not</i> love the kid. And guess what (OBVIOUS FACT ALERT) (cit.)? <b>I love him</b>! <br/><br/>•So now that we got the Obvious Fact out of the way, I should start listing all the rea</span>
  <span id="freeText660208524609029996" style="display:none"><b>"At this point, most people would have thrown themselves down on the ground and given up hope. And by most people, I mean me."</b><br><br>•I know that I have already raved plenty about how much I love this author and his characters, but <b>Magnus Chase</b> defies all standards of cutie-pie-ness and adorable-ness and funny-ness and whatnot. You just cannot <i>not</i> love the kid. And guess what (OBVIOUS FACT ALERT) (cit.)? <b>I love him</b>! <br><br>•So now that we got the Obvious Fact out of the way, I should start listing all the reasons why if you love Riordan and his previous books, you'll love this one too, and then those why if you have never read anything of his, you'll love it anyway. But I won't, partly because many of them already are in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1318210119?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">my review of <i>The Sword of Summer</i></a>, first book in The Gods of Asgard series, and partly because they can be more or less summed up in this sort of epiphany I had right after finishing this book: <b>I think that when Riordan writes a new book, the world becomes a little better place</b>. <br>His books are <b>fun</b> and <b>hilarious</b>. They are also utterly <b>brilliant</b> and <b>full of mythology</b> (yup, you might not have figured it out but that is kind of the point), which is cool and instructive for the children and <b>a real treat</b> for the mythology/history/this-kind-of-stuff freaks, and I know it first-hand now because I'm currently studying for a Germanic philology course and, being able to being up on all the gazillion <b>references</b>? Priceless. Plus, while they entertain you and teach you all this great stuff, <b>they also manage to tackle some sensitive and topical issue</b> on the side. Impossible, you say? <br>People, meet <b>Alex Fierro</b>.<br><br><b>"I’m gender fluid and transgender, idiot."</b><br><br>•And not only is Alex a great character as she (as said, Alex is gender fluid, but since in most of the scenes she appears as a female, I'll use this pronoun for convenience and because she made it clear that she doesn't do "they") represents <b>diversity</b> in such an unusual and compelling and absolutely perfect way, she is also <b>likeable</b>, <b>relatable</b>, <b>kick-ass</b> and a million shades of <b>splendid</b>. I also appreciated how the magical element intervenes in Alex's characterization -she's a shape-shifter, so she can be male one minute and female the next. Brilliant. And she and Magnus actually <i>talk</i> about what it means for her to be gender-fluid and how she feels about it. I think this is all the more perfect and astonishing when you consider that <i>The Hammer of Thor</i> is the second instalment in a <b>middle-grade</b> series. We need more writers like Rick Riordan.<br>Plus, I ship Alex and Magnus so hard you can't imagine.<br><br>•And now yes, <b>a couple of quotes for you</b> because I'm not that cold-hearted. <br><br><b>“The dragon’s mouth opened wide, revealing several extra rows of teeth—just in case the outer row of teeth didn’t kill me dead enough.”</b><br>---<br><b>“Hearth finger-spelled: K-E-N-N-I-N-G.<br>“What’s that?” I asked.<br>Samirah edged a little closer to the inscription. “A kenning is a Viking nickname.”<br>“You, mean like… Hey, Kenning. How’s it going?”</b><br>(My professor would have killed you so much, Magnus.)<br>---<br><b>“Dagfinn looked at me apologetically. “It's a Thing thing. You wouldn’t understand.”</b><br>---<br><b>“<i>Stop that</i>, I told my brain.<br><i>Also, the wedding is tomorrow</i>, said my brain.<br><i>Get out of my head.</i><br>My brain refused to get out of my head. Inconsiderate brain.”</b><br>---<br><b>“I think it's time you met Percy.”</b> And that must TOTALLY happen in the next book! Thumbs up for the <u>incoming crossover</u>! *happy dance*<br><br><br><b>PRE-READING</b><br><br>So, book, this is what I want from you:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452953598ra/17764892.gif" width="420" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Oh gods- sorry, wrong gif!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452953493ra/17764874.gif" width="420" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*mpfff*- okay, that's funny, but no!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425260302ra/13868778.gif" width="420" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yes. Yes, that's what I want. Evil <b>Loki</b> reigns.</span>
  <a data-text-id="660208524609029996" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1415335812" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1415335812" />
    <a title="ambsreads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30813900-ambsreads"><img alt="ambsreads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508924675p2/30813900.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1415335812?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ambsreads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ambsreads" href="/user/show/30813900-ambsreads">ambsreads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=magic">magic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1415335812" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1917704257444874739"><blockquote>
  <i>“Otis and his brother, Marvin, pulled the god’s chariot. They also provided Thor with a never-ending supply of goat meat. Each night, Thor killed and ate them for dinner. Each morning, Thor resurrected them. This is why you should go to college, kids—so when you grow up you do not have to take a job as a magical goat."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Rick Riordan's books are always some of my favourite books to read so <i>Magnus Chase and the Hammer of Thor</i> is no exception. That being said, it was even better than the first bo</span>
  <span id="freeText1917704257444874739" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“Otis and his brother, Marvin, pulled the god’s chariot. They also provided Thor with a never-ending supply of goat meat. Each night, Thor killed and ate them for dinner. Each morning, Thor resurrected them. This is why you should go to college, kids—so when you grow up you do not have to take a job as a magical goat."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Rick Riordan's books are always some of my favourite books to read so <i>Magnus Chase and the Hammer of Thor</i> is no exception. That being said, it was even better than the first book. The <i>Magnus Chase</i> series feels different from Rick Riordan's other books as well, I'm not sure if it's because Norse mythology is a whole lot more intense or because he uses a series of diverse characters, but it is beyond enjoyable to read. This book got so good that I stopped taking notes and recording quotes for my review because I had been excitedly telling people about this series and running around screaming. <br><br>Accurate representation of me:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1412971941ra/11450148.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now, what else can I say?<br>I don't even know what to say because I just dove straight into this book and if you have read the first one it may be the best plan of attack. <br><br><b>Diversity</b>. I will talk about diversity. Now, I noticed the other month when I joined Twitter for a short period of time people wanted diverse representations in YA fiction. <i>The Hammer of Thor</i> has this diversity. How? You may ask. Well, first we have Samirah al Abbas who is a Muslim character in the Norse world but also believes fully in Allah. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1475899364i/20780247._SX540_.png" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Sam's religion plays a large part in this series, with her prayers even being mentioned throughout this book. I studied Islam religion for two years in high school, so it is interesting to be able to use information I learnt in school to help me understand the book further. <br><br>However, Sam was in the first book so she isn't <b>that</b> big of a shock. The big shock of this book is Rick Riordan introducing the first gender-fluid character in his books, <b>Alex Fierro</b>. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1475899364i/20780248._SY540_.png" width="300" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I can say so much about Alex, but they were honestly my favourite character throughout this book. The fact that the pronouns were instantly taken on, whether Alex wanted to be called she/he, was amazing. I just loved it. <br><br>Now, I should probably talk about the plot and the world building. Everything in this book is just perfect. The fact that we have Magnus' witty sense of humour and other characters. The fact that Magnus makes mistakes and screams in situations. The fact that Magnus sucks at sword fighting. Now, that is just Magnus. The rest of the characters are developed so much further in this book. <br><br><b>This book doesn't suffer from second book syndrome.</b><br><br>The plot was completely action packed. I'm not sure there was a page where something <b>wasn't</b> happening, or if there was it was a chapter filled with humour that had me laughing incredibly loudly. <br><br>I mean the way that Rick winds his words together, because Magnus, is in fact, Annabeth's cousin, is beautiful. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“I’d even had a mind-melting conversation with my cousin Annabeth about the Greek gods who hung out in New York and made her life difficult. Apparently North America was lousy with ancient gods. We had a full-blown infestation."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>I'm not even sure what else to say, this whole review is a complete mess. I am a mess. I love this series so much. I think the only thing that could have made this book better if our Thor was more like this <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475899364ra/20780249.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>You can't live in my household, where my mum is so obsessed with Thor/Chris Hemsworth that our dog got named Thor, without loving the man too. <br><br>Overall, this book is a masterpiece and is definitely on my favourites of 2016 list.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1917704257444874739" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3144536063" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3144536063" />
    <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani"><img alt="Ahmad Sharabiani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194930432p2/614778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3144536063?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ahmad Sharabiani" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani">Ahmad Sharabiani</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=21th-century">21th-century</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3144536063" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5242048609889972691"><b>The Hammer of Thor (Magnus Chase and the Gods of Asgard #2), Rick Riordan</b><br/><br/>The Hammer of Thor is an American young-adult fantasy novel based on Norse mythology written by Rick Riordan. It was published on October 4, 2016. <br/><br/>The book opens six weeks after the close of the preceding novel, The Sword of Summer. <br/><br/>Magnus Chase meets with Samirah "Sam" al-Abbas and Otis, one of the god Thor's two goats, who inform the heroes Thor's hammer is still missing.<br/><br/>The jötnar are beginning to suspect Thor does not h</span>
  <span id="freeText5242048609889972691" style="display:none"><b>The Hammer of Thor (Magnus Chase and the Gods of Asgard #2), Rick Riordan</b><br /><br />The Hammer of Thor is an American young-adult fantasy novel based on Norse mythology written by Rick Riordan. It was published on October 4, 2016. <br /><br />The book opens six weeks after the close of the preceding novel, The Sword of Summer. <br /><br />Magnus Chase meets with Samirah "Sam" al-Abbas and Otis, one of the god Thor's two goats, who inform the heroes Thor's hammer is still missing.<br /><br />The jötnar are beginning to suspect Thor does not have his weapon to defend Midgard and plan to invade. On Otis's advice, Sam and Magnus visit a Norse barrow in Provincetown. Magnus returns to Hotel Valhalla to rest and prepare, where he meets Alex Fierro, Sam's newest einherji recruit and a genderfluid child of Loki. While in Valhalla, Magnus has dreamlike visions of Loki manipulating his uncle Randolph. <br /><br />Loki also tells Magnus about a wedding between Samirah and the giant Thrym in five days, and that Magnus will need to bring the bride-price. Magnus, Sam, and their friends Blitzen and Hearthstone travel to the Provincetown barrow but discover the Skofnung Sword instead of Thor's hammer. Loki appears and tells the quartet the sword and matching whetstone will be Sam's bride-price. They are reluctant to help Loki, who causes Randolph Chase to wound Blitzen with the sword.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش روز شانزدهم ماه ژانویه سال 2019میلادی<br /><br />عنوان چکش ثور؛ نویسنده: ریک ریوردان؛ مترجم آرزو مقدس؛ تهران، نشر پرتقال‏‫، 1397؛ در 500صفحه، شابک 9786004621236؛ موضوع داستانهای نویسندگان ایالات متحده آمریکا - سده 21م<br /><br />عنوان چکش ثور؛ نویسنده ریک ریوردان؛ مترجم: وحید جعفری‌ منصوریان؛ تهران، انتشارات بهنام، ‏‫1397؛ در 448ص؛ شابک 9786007132500؛<br /><br />مکنوس چیس در نبردی خونین و بی‌ترحم با غول آتش، جان میبازد، و سپس در هتل «والهالا» در پیکره‌ ی یکی از جنگجویان «اودین»، حیاتی دوباره پیدا میکند، به جهان چشم میگشاید؛ این زندگی دوباره فرصتی برای در آرامش زیستن اوست؛ امیدوار هست؛ او از «اوتیس» خبرچین سراغ گمشده را میگیرد، و نام «پراونیس تاون» قاتلی با نقاب گرگ را میشنود، که به او هشدار میدهد، جستجو برای یافتن چکش را رها کند، زیرا چکش در زیر زمین است، و با جادویی توانمند و مهلک نگهداری می‌شود، و از دیگر سو، ارتش غول‌ها نیز بسیج شده‌ اند تا حمله کنند، و اگر نتواند چکش را بیابد، آنان جهان را به نابودی کشیده و جهان‌های نه‌ گانه را زیر و رو خواهند کرد...؛ <br /><br />نمونه متن (درس لیاردین اگر یک والکایری را بیرون، به یک قهوه دعوت کنید، چیزی که روی دستتان خواهد ماند، یک صورتحساب و یک جنازه خواهد بود؛ سَمیرا آل عباس را حدودا شش هفته بود که ندیده بودم و زمانیکه با من تماس گرفت و گفت میخواهد درباره یک موضوع مرگ و زندگی با من صحبت کند، فورا قبول کردم؛ در واقع، من مرده بودم و این یعنی، موضوع مرگ و زندگی در مورد من صدق نمیکرد اما سَم مضطرب به نظر میرسید؛ زمانیکه به کافه تینکینگ کاپ در خیابان نیوبری رسیدم، او هنوز نیامده بود؛ کافه طبق معمول شلوغ بود و من مجبور شدم برای یک فنجان قهوه در صف بایستم؛ چند دقیقه بعد سَم مثل اجل معلق جلوتر از همه در صف ظاهر شد؛ هیچکس ککش هم نگزید؛ آدمهای معمولی زیاد متوجه این چیزهای جادویی نمیشوند که این خودش جای شکر دارد چون در غیر اینصورت اهالی بوستون بیشتر وقت خود را با ترس و وحشت از غولها، جنها، اِلفها و اُرکها در حال دویدن به این طرف و آن طرف خواهند بود؛ اینهریارها با آن تبرزینهای جنگی را نیز باید اضافه کنم سَم با لباس فرم مدرسه در کنارم نشست؛ کتانی سفید، شلوار خاکی نظامی و یک پیراهن آستین بلند ملوانی با آرم آکادمی کینگ به تن داشت، با حجاب سبزی موهایش را پوشانده بود و تبرزینی به کمربندنش آویزان کرده بود؛ <br /><br />با نگاه اول میشد فهمید آن تبرزین اصلاً مناسب قد و قواره اش نیست، همچنان که از دیدنش خوشحال بودم، متوجه کبودی زیر چشمهایش شدم که کمی غیرعادی به نظر میرسید؛ او داشت روی پاهایش این طرف و آن طرف تاب میخورد؛ گفتم «هی، وحشتناک به نظر میای.» گفت «مگنوس، من هم از دیدنت خوشحالم» - نه، منظورم وحشتناک نه به اون معنی ...؛ منظورم اینه که خسته و به هم ریخته ای؛ - بس کن دیگه ...؛ دستهایم را به نشانه تسلیم بالا بردم و گفتم «تو این مدت کجا بودی؟» کمی خود را جمع وجور کرد و گفت «این ترم کارام خیلی زیاد شده و داره منو از پا درمیاره. بعد از مدرسه به بچه ها درس میدم؛ نمیدونم یادته یا نه، یه شغل پاره وقت هم دارم که جمع کردن ارواح مرده ها و انجام ماموریت سرّی برای اودینه» - اوه.؛ چقدر سرت شلوغه؛ - از اینا گذشته، یه دوره پرواز هم میرم؛ - دوره پرواز؟ با هواپیما؟؛<br /><br />میدانستم که سَم آرزو داشت روزی یک خلبان حرفه ای شود ولی متوجه نشده بودم در حال گذراندن دوره مخصوص پرواز باشد؛ گفتم «خوبه که تو شونزده سالگی میتونی این همه کار انجام بدی» چشمهایش از هیجان برق زد و گفت «پدر بزرگ و مادربزرگم هیچ وقت توان مالی شو نداشتن ولی خانواده فدلان یه دوستی دارن که یه مدرسه پرواز رو اداره میکنه؛ اونا هم جید و بی بی رو سر این موضوع قانع کردن» با پوزخند گفتم «آهان پس درسها و دوره ها یه هدیه از طرف امیره؛ گونه هایش سرخ شد؛ او تنها نوجوانی بود که میدیدم در این سن نامزد دارد و برای من جالب بود زمانی که درباره امیر فدلان حرف میزند، چقدر دستپاچه و مضطرب میشود؛ سَم آهی کشید و گفت «اون درسها و دوره ها بیش از حد متفکرانه بودن، اما دیگه کافیه؛ من تو رو اینجا نیاوردم درباره مشغله ی من صحبت کنیم؛ یه خبرچین دارم که باید ببینیش» - یه خبرچین؟ - این همون لحظه ای میتونه باشه که منتظرش بودم؛ البته خدا کنه خبراش به درد بخور باشه؛ صدای زنگ تلفن سَم بلند شد؛ گوشی تلفن خود را از جیبش بیرون آورد، به صفحه نمایش آن نگاه کرد و گفت «اه، لعنتی! باید برم» - تو که تازه اومدی؛ - این یه قضیه والکایریه؛ کد احتمالی سه - هشت - یک، یعنی یه مرگ حماسی در حال وقوعه؛ - این داستانها چیه داری میبافی؟ - داستان نیست؛ - خب ...؛ که چی، یکی که فکر میکنه داره میمیره، به تو پیامک میفرسته که ما داریم میمیریم و در اسرع وقت نیاز به والکایری داریم! و به دنبالش هم چند تا از این شکلکهای غمگین میفرسته؛ - یادم باشه یه بار دیگه روح تو رو به والهالا ببرم؛ تو به من پیامک نزده بودی؛ - هر چی باشه من یه شخص خاص هستم؛ - یه میز بیرون رزرو کن و خبرچین منو ببین؛ من زود برمیگردم، - من حتی نمیدونم این خبرچین چه شکلیه؛ - وقتی ببینیش، میشناسیش؛ شجاع باش؛ یه دونه از اون بیسکوئیتها هم به من بده؛ <br /><br />سپس پرواز کرد و از کافه خارج شد و من ماندم و صورتحساب کافه؛ دو فنجان بزرگ قهوه و دو عدد بیسکوییت گرفتم و پشت میزی در بیرون کافه نشستم؛ امسال، بهار در شهر بوستون کمی زودتر از سالهای قبل رسیده بود؛ لکه های کثیف برف هنوز روی لبه پیاده راه ها مثل کثیفی و جرم روی دندان دیده میشد؛ اما غنچه های سفید و قرمز؛ درختان گیلاس بر روی شاخ و برگها پراکنده بودند؛ لباسهای گل منگلی از پشت ویترین یک لباس فروشی طوری به نظر رسید که انگار شکوفه داده باشند؛ توریستها در حال لذت بردن از نور آفتاب بودند؛ خارج از کافه نشسته بودم و در شلوار جین، تی شرت و پیراهنی که تازه از خشک شویی گرفته بودم، احساس راحتی میکردم؛ با خود فکر کردم بعد از سه سال این اولین بهاری است که آواره و آلاخون والاخون نیستم؛ <br /><br />همین ماه مارس گذشته داشتم داخل آهن قراضه ها جان میکندم و زیر پل پابلیک گاردن میخوابیدم؛ با دوستان عزیزم هارت و بلیتز) بیرون میرفتم و همگی سعی میکردیم گیر پلیس نیفتیم؛ فقط میخواستیم زنده بمانیم؛ دو ماه قبل، در مبارزه با غول آتش کشته شده بودم و وقتی بیدار شدم، خودم را در هتل والهالا دیدم؛ من یکی از جنگجویان اینهریار اودین شده بودم، اکنون لباسهای تمیز به تن میکردم، روزی نبود که دوش نگیرم و شبی نبود که روی تخت گرم و نرم نخوابم؛ میتوانستم در این کافه و سر این میز بنشینم و چیزی بخورم که واقعا پول آن را پرداخت کرده ام، بدون نگرانی از اینکه من را از کافه اخراج کنند؛ از زمان تولد دوباره، به چیزهای عجیب و غریب فراوانی عادت کرده بودم، در جهانهای نُه گانه سیر کرده بودم؛ خدایان نورس، اِلفها و کوتوله ها را دیده بودم؛ هیولاهایی را مشاهده کرده بودم که حتی تلفظ نام آنها نیز برایم دشوار است؛ یک شمشیر جادویی نیز به من اعطا شده بود که آن را به شکل یک آویز به گردنم انداخته ام؛ حتی یک مکالمه با دخترخاله ام، آنابت درباره خدایان یونانی داشتم که نیویورک را پاتوق خود کرده، زندگی را برایش دشوار کرده بودند؛ ظاهرا آمریکای شمالی مملو از خدایان باستانی اکبیری شده بود و ما تحت هجمه ای همه جانبه قرار داشتیم؛ <br /><br />من همه اینها را قبول داشتم؛ حالا به بوستون برگشته بودم و در یک روز خوب بهاری، اینجا مثل یک آدم معمولی نشسته بودم؛ درست است...؛ میدانم کمی عجیب است؛ در افراد پیرامونم کمی دقت کردم تا شاید بتوانم خبرچین سَم را تشخیص بدهم؛ او گفته بود به محض اینکه اونو ببینی، میشناسیش؛ با خود گفتم، این شخص چه اطلاعاتی میتواند داشته باشد که برای سَم حکم مرگ و زندگی را داشت؛ چشمهایم بر یک نقطه روی سر در مغازه ای قفل شد؛ سر در مغازه یک تابلوی نقره ای - برنجی بود که روی آن نوشته شده بود «بهترین بلیتزن» اما کرکره ی مغازه پایین بود و روی شیشه پنجره ی جلویی نوشته شده بود برای تغییر دکوراسیون تعطیل است؛ امیدوار بودم بتوانم از سَم درباره ی او سئوال کنم؛ نمیدانم چرا دوست قدیمی من، بلیتز ناگهان غیبش زده بود؛ <br /><br />همین چند هفته پیش داشتم از جلوی مغازه اش رد میشدم که فهمیدم بسته است؛ بعد از آن دیگر هیچ خبری از بلیتز و هارت نشد که نشد؛ این قضیه حسابی فکرم را مشغول کرده بود و موضوع خبرچین پاک داشت از یادم میرفت که ناگهان او را بالای سرم دیدم؛ حق با سَم بود؛ دیدن یک بُز که بارانی پوشیده باشد، چیزی نیست که آدم هر روز در خیابان ها مشاهده کند؛ کلاهی بر سر داشت که دو شاخش از آن بیرون زده بود؛ عینک آفتابی هم زده بود؛ بارانیش مانع از آن میشد که سُمهای سیاهش دیده شود؛ با همه اینها، فورا او را شناختم. من این بُز را در دنیای دیگر کشته و خورده بودم و این یک تجربه فراموش نشدنی بود؛ گفتم «اوتیس ...!» گفت: «ش...؛ ش...؛ ششش...؛ یواشتر، من ناشناسم؛ ولی خب، منو همون اوتیس صدا کن»؛<br /><br />فورا بر روی صندلی ای که برای سَم رزرو کرده بودم، پرید و لَم داد؛ سُم هایش را روی میز انداخت و به خیال اینکه سَم داخل پاکت شیرینی قایم شده، به پاکت خیره شد و گفت «والکایری کجاس؟ نکنه اونم ناشناسه...؛» گفتم «سَم باید میرفت جایی ...؛ دنبال یه روح؛ گفت زود برمیگرده ...؛» اوتیس با افسوس گفت «اوه، باید زندگی یه هدف و معنایی داشته باشه؛ برای غذا ممنونم»؛ گفتم «اون برای تو نبود»؛ بیسکوئیت سَم را برداشت و همه آن را خورد؛ حتی کاغذ و جعبه اش را؛ زن و مرد میانسالی که پشت میز کناریمان نشسته بودند، به این رفیق بُز من نگاه میکردند و لبخند میزدند؛ احتمالا حس انسانی آنها اوتیس را به شکل یک سگ خانگی یا یک بچه بامزه میدید؛ همچنان که در حال جویدن جعبه بیسکوئیت بود و خرده های آن روی لباسش میریخت؛<br /><br />به او گفتم: «خب، ظاهرا یه چیزایی برای گفتن داری.» بادگلویی زد و گفت «موضوع اَربابم درمیونه» گفتم «ثور...!» کمی به خود پیچید و گفت «آره، ثور...؛» راستش اگر من هم برای خدای توفان کار میکردم، وقتی اسم ثور به میان میآمد به خود میپیچیدم؛ وظیفه اوتیس و برادرش، ماروین، کشیدن کالسکه خدای توفان بود؛ آنها همچنین منبع غذایی بی پایانی برای ثور بودند؛ ثور هر شب آنها را سربریده و برای شام نوش جان میکرد و صبح روز بعد دوباره آنها زنده میشدند؛ اینجا معلوم میشود که چرا شما باید به کالج بروید تا بزرگ که شدید، مجبور نباشید شغلی مثل این بُز جادویی را انتخاب کنید؛<br /><br />اوتیس گفت «باید بگم اون شیء مخصوص اربابم گم شده» - منظورت چکشه...؟ «- یواشتر بگو...»؛ آره، منظورم همون چکشه؛ ماه ژانویه را به خاطر آوردم، وقتی که خدای توفان را برای اولین بار ملاقات میکردم روزهای خوبی بود؛ کنار آتش...؛ گوش دادن به حرفهای ثور که درباره برنامه های تلویزیونی مورد علاقه اش و همین طور از چکش گم شده اش میگفت که از آن برای کشتن غولها و دیدن برنامه های تلویزیونی استفاده میکرد؛ از اوتیس پرسیدم «هنوز پیداش نکرده؟» اوتیس سُمهایش را روی میز کشید و گفت «راستشو بخوای، نه...؛ اگه غولها بدونن که ثور اون چیزی رو که من و تو میدونیم، نداره؛ اونوقته که به دنیای آدما حمله کنن و همه چیز رو نابود کنن؛ ماههاست که داریم میگردیم؛ دشمنای ثور دارن گستاخ میشن؛ اونا این ضعف رو حس کردن؛ به دکتر روانشناسم گفتم این قضیه منو یاد بچگیهام میندازه، که بچه های قلدر اذیتم میکردن»؛<br /><br />چشمهای اوتیس از شدت نگرانی برق میزد؛ این قضیه بهانه ای شد، تا ساعتها با اوتیس راجع به احساساتش حرف بزنم؛ به او گفتم من احساسات و حالش را درک میکنم؛ گفتم «اوتیس یادمه بار آخری که همدیگه رو دیدیم، ثور یه چوب دستی بلند داشت که ازش به عنوان یه سلاح پشتیبان استفاده میکرد؛ ثور کاملاً هم بی دفاع نیست»؛ جواب داد «آره، ولی اون چوبدستی جای چکش رو نمیگیره؛ راستش رو بخوای چوبدستی، ترس و وحشت لازم رو تو دل غولها نمیندازه؛ تازه، وقتی ثور برنامه های مورد علاقه اش رو از طریق اون میبینه، بدخلق میشه»؛<br /><br />اصلا دوست نداشتم ثور را بدخلق ببینم، خیلی از حرفهای اوتیس با عقل جور درنمیآمد؛ مثلاً اینکه چرا ثور قادر نبود چکش را در یک جای امن نگهداری کند و اینکه او چطور توانسته بود قضیه گم شدن چکش را تا این حد سرّی نگه دارد هم جالب بود؛ با تردید گفتم «پس ثور الان به کمک ما نیاز داره؟» اوتیس گفت «نه به طور رسمی!» گفتم «البته که نه...؛ همگی باید بارونی بپوشیم و عینک دودی بزنیم!»؛<br /><br />به کنایه جواب داد «فکر خوبیه...؛» و ادامه داد «در هر حال، به والکایری گفتم اونو در جریان کارا قرار میدم؛ او داره ماموریتی مخصوص رو برای اودین انجام میده؛ این اولین سرنخیه که از محل اختفای اون شیء مخصوص پیدا کردم؛ منبع خبر، موثقه.؛ یه بُز دیگه هست که پیش همون دکتر روانشناسی میره که من میرم، و یه چیزایی به گوشش خورده»؛ گفتم «خب، حالا تو از ما میخوای براساس یه چیزایی که تو اتاق انتظار روانکاوت گفته و شنیده شده، بریم جلو؟»؛ اوتیس طوری به صندلی لم داد، که نزدیک بود از صندلی بیفتد، و گفت «این عالیه...؛ فقط باید خیلی مراقب باشیم»؛<br /><br />خیلی تلاش کردم جلوی خنده ام را بگیرم؛ من با غولها بازی گرفتن توپهای مذاب را انجام میدادم؛ بر فراز بوستون مثل عقاب پرواز میکردم؛ مار عظیم الجثه و معروف را، از ماساچوست بیرون کرده بودم، فنریس گرگ را، با یک توپ نخ شکست داده بودم، و حالا یک الف بچه، به من میگفت مراقب باشم؛<br /><br />پرسیدم «خب...؛ حالا این چکش کجا میتونه باشه؟ در جوتانهایم؟ در نفلهایم؟ یا در ثورفارهایم؟»؛ اوتیس که عینک آفتابی اش کمی به پایین دماغش لغزیده بود، گفت «راستش رو بخوای چکش در یه محل خطرناک قرار گرفته...؛ تو پراوینستون»؛ گفتم «پراوینستون؟ بالای قله کیپ کاد؟»؛<br /><br />خاطرات مبهمی راجع به آن محل داشتم؛ وقتی شش سالم بود، مادرم در یکروز تابستانی آخر هفته مرا به آن اطراف برده بود؛ ساحل، رولت خرچنگ، آب نباتها و گالریهای هنری آنجا را هنوز به یاد دارم؛ خطرناکترین چیزی که آنروز با آن مواجه شدیم، یک مرغ دریایی بود که به سندرم حاد روده مبتلا شده بود؛ دیگر خودتان فکرش را بکنید؛ اوتیس با صدای آرامی گفت «یه بارو توی پراوینستون هست که مال یه ویگته، ویگت یه موجود قدرتمنده که سلاحهای جادویی رو از همه جا برای خودش جمع میکنه؛ به مقبره ی یه ویگت، میگن بارو؛ ببخشید، وقتی درباره ویگتها حرف میزنم یه جوری میشم؛ اونا منو یاد پدرم میندازن»؛<br /><br />طبیعتا با حرفهایی که اوتیس زد دوباره سئوالهایی درباره کودکی او به ذهنم خطور کرد ولی ترجیح دادم اینبار آنها را به روانکاوش واگذار کنم؛ پرسیدم «وایکینگهای زیادی تو پراوینستون هستن؟»؛ جواب داد «تا اونجا که من میدونم، فقط یه دونه هست؛ اما همون یه دونه هم کافیه؛ اگه اون چیزی که ما دنبالش هستیم اونجا باشه، به سختی میشه پسش گرفت؛ چون زیر زمینه و توسط نگهبانای جادویی محافظت میشه؛ در اینصورت تو به دوستات، کوتوله ها و اِلفها نیاز خواهی داشت»؛<br /><br />راستش اگر میدانستم دوستانی که اوتیس میگفت، کجا هستند؛ عالی میشد؛ امیدوار بودم سَم درباره ی آنها اطلاعاتی داشته باشد؛پرسیدم «خب...؛ چرا ثور خودش نمیره بارو رو چک کنه؟ وایسا، بذار حدس بزنم؛ اون نمیخواد جلب توجه کنه...؛ یا اینکه میخواد یه فرصتی به ما بده.؛ یا شاید، چون اینکار واقعا سخته»؛ اوتیس گفت «راستش رو بخوای سری جدید جسیکا جونز هنوز شروع نشده»؛ به خودم گفتم خطای بزرگی نیست، حقش نیست که مشتی تو چونه اش بخوره؛ گفتم «خوبه...؛ پس سَم که بیاد اینجا درباره نقشه مون حرف میزنیم»؛ گفت «بعید میدونم بتونم اینجا منتظرش باشم ...؛ باید زودتر از این به تو میگفتم؛ یه کسی ...؛ یا یه چیزی داره منو میپاد»؛ کمی جا خوردم و گفتم «یعنی میگی تو رو تا اینجا دنبال کردن؟»؛ جواب داد «مطمئن نیستم ...؛ باید امیدوار باشیم که این تغییر قیافه اونا رو گمراه کرده باشه»؛ گفتم «اوه، چه عالی!» خیابان را بررسی کردم اما کسی یا چیزی را که اوتیس میگفت، ندیدم؛ ...؛)؛ پایان نقل از متن<br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 18/06/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>
  <a data-text-id="5242048609889972691" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1478432310" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1478432310?book_show_action=true">Dec 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=great-but-not-quite-there-yet">great-but-not-quite-there-yet</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1478432310" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer7052938337738480911">Nice Natalie: I don't like that we're <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1394786091' rel='nofollow noopener'>always </a> here these days with Riordan's books.<br/><br/>Cynical Natalie: Maybe if he wrote quality material, we wouldn't be here. Exhibit A: the plot. Hello, quest-with-sidekicks narrative 65.0.<br/><br/>Nice Natalie: Oh, come on, you liked the plot! You laughed a bunch of times.<br/><br/>Cynical Natalie: I laugh at Vines, but that doesn't mean they deserve an Oscar. What about Hearthstone's dad? <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[They basically left him there, half-mad and terrorizing his guests. <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoi</a></span></span>
  <span id="freeText7052938337738480911" style="display:none">Nice Natalie: I don't like that we're <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1394786091" rel="nofollow noopener">always </a> here these days with Riordan's books.<br><br>Cynical Natalie: Maybe if he wrote quality material, we wouldn't be here. Exhibit A: the plot. Hello, quest-with-sidekicks narrative 65.0.<br><br>Nice Natalie: Oh, come on, you liked the plot! You laughed a bunch of times.<br><br>Cynical Natalie: I laugh at Vines, but that doesn't mean they deserve an Oscar. What about Hearthstone's dad? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[They basically left him there, half-mad and terrorizing his guests. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> That plot thread is so loose, people keep mistaking it for the word "lose."<br><br>Nice Natalie: They were on a tight schedule. I'm sure they'll get back to it next book.<br><br>Cynical Natalie: And don't even get me started on the ending.<br><br>Nice Natalie: Oh boy, here we go. *takes cover*<br><br>Cynical Natalie: <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"I think it's time you met Percy." </i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1459631721ra/18637411.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Percy. Fucking. Jackson. He has to be dragged into every damn series, every damn mythology now, does he? We all know why—The Kane Chronicles bombed without Percy. The fans want Percy, so Riordan's going to keep extending the franchise and stabbing Easter eggs in places Poseidon's son has no business being.<br><br>And people are eating it up! Oh, my God, hardly <i>anyone</i> is complaining about this. Why are we sitting by and letting this blatant fanservice sneak by?<br><br>Nice Natalie: Maybe because, like us, they squealed with delight during that part and maybe because, like us, it's the main reason they're excited for the next book.<br><br>Cynical Natalie: ...Shut up. <br><br>Nice Natalie: Can we talk about the good stuff now? There's a transgender and gender fluid love interest. How awesome is that?<br><br>Cynical Natalie: Yes, and the reveal was about as subtle as a haddock to the face. Sam told us outright that she's transgender. It's lazy writing.<br><br>Nice Natalie: It's a middle-grade book. A good portion of adults don't understand the gender spectrum beyond gay, lesbian, and bisexual. This way, the message clearly comes across. <br><br>Culture appropriation is mentioned, too. It seems as though Riordan is finally getting a handle on this diversity thing. It felt a little for show in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26252859.The_Hidden_Oracle__The_Trials_of_Apollo___1_" title="The Hidden Oracle (The Trials of Apollo, #1) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hidden Oracle</a>, but here, we get to see Sam pray and interact with her culture. Nothing against Muslim-Americans who don't feel strongly about their religion, of course, but in the wake of the election and all these hate crimes going on, it's nice to see a Muslim American character who indulges in these belief and still be portrayed positively. She's someone we can root for, not a fear-monger's terrorist. <br><br>This line is beautiful: <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"I wondered how Inge felt about being required to show her tail at all times. Was it a source of pride to show her identity , or did it feel like a punishment?"</i>
</blockquote> <br><br>Respectful, thoughtful while leaving room for personal consideration. <br><br>Cynical Natalie: You think you have me beat, don't you?<br><br>Nice Natalie: Nice girls don't engage in competition, but yes.<br><br>Cynical Natalie: ...Fuck you.<br><br>Nice Natalie: I love you, too.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481771342ra/21453650.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/903559999" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of The Sword of Summer</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1478432316" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of The Ship of the Dead</a><br><br>Other Nice Natalie/Cynical Natalie <s>brawls</s> reviews:<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/372646324" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fault in Our Stars</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/989706383" rel="nofollow noopener">A Girl Like You</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/915207283" rel="nofollow noopener">If I Stay</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/940598996" rel="nofollow noopener">Dreams of Gods &amp; <div id="review_1777040693" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1777040693" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1777040693?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1777040693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17804101597913030104">Thor's lost his dang hammer again.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1477000058ra/20906308.gif' width='300' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>Loki is scheming and causing trouble, again.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1477000446ra/20906332.gif' width='300' height='192' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>3.5 stars. Final review, first posted on <a href='http://www.fantasyliterature.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fantasy Literature</a>:<br/><br/>The god Thor has lost his hammer again, but this time it’s even worse: the giant Thrym has gotten hold of it and has hidden it away where no one else can reach it. If the hammer isn’t returned to Thor quickly, enemies of Asgard will take advantage of their weakness and attack, triggering Ragnarok, the battle at the end of the world, and bringing massive deat</span>
  <span id="freeText17804101597913030104" style="display:none">Thor's lost his dang hammer again.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1477000058ra/20906308.gif" width="300" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Loki is scheming and causing trouble, again.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1477000446ra/20906332.gif" width="300" height="192" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>3.5 stars. Final review, first posted on <a href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantasy Literature</a>:<br><br>The god Thor has lost his hammer again, but this time it’s even worse: the giant Thrym has gotten hold of it and has hidden it away where no one else can reach it. If the hammer isn’t returned to Thor quickly, enemies of Asgard will take advantage of their weakness and attack, triggering Ragnarok, the battle at the end of the world, and bringing massive death and destruction in the Nine Worlds.<br><br>Loki the trickster, who has been chained up by the other gods as punishment for his misdeeds, visits Magnus Chase in a dream (Loki gets around pretty well in dreamland). He tells Magnus that he’s worked out a deal to get Thor’s hammer back: all Magnus has to do is bring Thrym a certain bride for a wedding in five days, along with the bride-price, and Thrym will give back the hammer as his wedding gift.<br><br>There are just a few problems with this plan: The intended bride is the Valkyrie Samirah, Magnus’ friend and Loki’s daughter, who is already engaged to another man and, by the way, has absolutely no interest in marrying a giant. The bride-price that Magnus is supposed to bring to the giant is the magical Skofnung Sword, hidden in a mummified Danish king’s tomb and protected by zombie Viking guards. And certainly not least is the fact that Loki certainly has a scheme, his own devious reason for brokering this deal … if only Magnus could figure out what it is. But Magnus doesn’t see any choice but to go along with the plan, at least for now. Luckily he has his friends Samirah, Blitzen the fashion-forward dwarf, and the elf Hearthstone to help him, as well as a new acquaintance, Alex Fierro, the latest addition to the halls of Valhalla.<br><br><i>The Hammer of Thor</i> (2016) doesn’t diverge from Rick Riordan’s formula of mythological gods and smart-aleck half-blood children who are sent off on various quests and adventures in each book, but Riordan excels at telling a fast-paced, humorous adventure. Magnus’ talkative sword Sumarbrander, the Sword of Summer (fondly known as “Jack”) is back in full force, chatting with Magnus, flying through the air to fight enemies all by himself, and ill-advisedly falling in love with the lovely and deadly Skofnung Sword. Samirah and Hearthstone both become more fully fleshed out characters, as we get to know more about their lives and backgrounds, particularly when we visit Hearthstone’s family home in Alfheim. Thor’s hammer strikes me as a bit of a MacGuffin, an object whose primary function is to advance the plot, and, entertaining as it was, I’m not certain the overarching plot of this series was advanced much in this middle book. While the plot is amusing and we explore a few more of the Nine Worlds, the entire book struck me as a rather elaborate way to set up just one particular event that occurs toward the end.<br><br>The most notable difference from his earlier books is that Riordan is making an appreciable effort to include more diverse characters, particularly in the MAGNUS CHASE AND THE GODS OF ASGARD series: Magnus is a formerly homeless teen, Hearthstone the elf is deaf, and Magnus’s closest companion is Samirah, a devout Muslim. Now in <i>The Hammer of Thor</i> we meet the gender-fluid Alex, whose self-identification as either male or female can change from day to day. Like Samirah, Alex is a child of the trickster god Loki, who in the traditional Norse legends was able to change his sex: he often disguised himself as a woman. So it does make sense for Loki to have a gender-fluid child. There’s a slightly clunky lecturing tone to Magnus’ discussions with Alex about respecting Alex’s current gender choice and calling Alex by the gender he/she currently identifies as, but overall this somewhat touchy subject is handled sensitively and in a way that most will consider appropriate for its intended age group of readers.<br><br>The MAGNUS CHASE AND THE GODS OF ASGARD series is generally light-hearted and humorous, though it does include a fair amount of violence and mayhem, in a nod to the warlike Viking culture that inspires this series. Most of the time the violence is played for comic effect, so it’s not likely to traumatize any but the most sensitive readers. <i>The Hammer of Thor</i> is a solid story; it might not appeal to readers who are tired of Riordan’s formula, but it will almost certainly please the Riordan fan in your house.<br><br><i>I received a free copy of this book from the publisher in exchange for a review. Thank you!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="17804101597913030104" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
